{"code":1,"isDone":false,"toInsertArticleList":[{"createdTime":"2021-07-13 02:35:16","updatedTime":"2021-07-13 02:35:16","title":"‘Stranger Things’ Season 4 Will Reveal a “Very Big” Secret About Hopper That David Harbour Has Known Since Season 1","link":"https://www.slashfilm.com/?p=682780","description":"<p><img class=\"alignnone size-medium wp-image-603510 aligncenter\" src=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/stranger-things-4-hopper-700x314.jpg\" alt=\"stranger things 4 teaser\" width=\"700\" height=\"314\" srcset=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/stranger-things-4-hopper-700x314.jpg 700w, https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/stranger-things-4-hopper-360x161.jpg 360w, https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/stranger-things-4-hopper-768x344.jpg 768w, https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/stranger-things-4-hopper.jpg 1440w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 700px) 100vw, 700px\" /></p>\n<p>Last time we all saw <em><strong>Stranger Things</strong></em><em>&#8216; </em>Jim Hopper, he appeared to be getting blown to smithereens inside an underground Russian scientific facility. However, <a href=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/stranger-things-2-bob/\">unlike poor Bob</a> (<strong>Sean Astin</strong>), Hopper survived his apparent onscreen death, appearing in a post-credit sequence that teased his continued existence. While stars <strong>Finn Wolfhard </strong>and <strong>Joe Keery</strong> have <a href=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/stranger-things-season-4-update/\">already hinted that season 4 will be the &#8220;darkest season yet&#8221;</a>, now we have some confirmation from Big Daddy Hopper himself.</p>\n<p><span id=\"more-682780\"></span></p>\n<p><img class=\"size-medium wp-image-682797 aligncenter\" src=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/elevencellar-700x300.jpg\" alt=\"\" width=\"700\" height=\"300\" srcset=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/elevencellar.jpg 700w, https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/elevencellar-360x154.jpg 360w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 700px) 100vw, 700px\" /></p>\n<h2>Boxes in the Attic</h2>\n<p>In a recent interview with <a href=\"https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=04Rr0u0fj_E\">Entertainment Weekly</a>, <strong>David Harbour</strong>, who portrays Sheriff Hopper on the Netflix hit, said that this season will finally dig into his many secrets.</p>\n<p>&#8220;There&#8217;s some fun stuff that we&#8217;re doing this season, but it&#8217;s also the heaviest dramatic stuff I&#8217;ve ever had to do,&#8221; Harbour said.</p>\n<p>Season 3 Hooper had a lot on his plate. He was trying to handle his adopted teenage daughter&#8217;s first romance while still being a good dad, figure out what the Russians were doing beneath the mall, and also deal with the forces of evil coming into the town of Hawkins from the Upside Down. He survived all of that, and getting blown up, just to get taken captive by the Russians.</p>\n<p>&#8220;[He was] this guy who&#8217;s struggling with his teenage daughter and sort of trapped in this world of his own darkness, [&#8230;] he&#8217;s going to re-emerge as a different human being,&#8221; Harbour said. &#8220;In that way, he has this vulnerability to him, and also this brutality that he needs to survive Russia. We get to see this whole other side of him and it&#8217;s some of my favorite stuff.&#8221;</p>\n<p>Part of getting to see that other side of him is a reveal that has been building since season 1, Harbour hinted.</p>\n<blockquote><p>&#8220;We get to see a lot of Hopper at his most vulnerable, we&#8217;re gonna reveal a lot of backstory points that we&#8217;ve only hinted at in boxes in his attic. We&#8217;re gonna see a lot of these different threads, and also, we get to see a rebirth of him.&#8221;</p></blockquote>\n<p>The &#8220;boxes in the attic&#8221; Harbour refers to are from the season 2 episode &#8220;Will the Wise.&#8221; While cleaning out their shared cabin, his adoptive daughter Eleven (<strong>Millie Bobby Brown</strong>) discovers mysterious boxes labeled &#8220;Dad,&#8221; &#8220;New York,&#8221; &#8220;Vietnam,&#8221; and &#8220;Hawkins Lab&#8221; in a hidden cellar. (Attic, cellar, same difference right?) Eleven grabbed the Hawkins Lab box and gave us all a peek inside, but the contents of the other three boxes are still a mystery.</p>\n<p><img class=\"size-medium wp-image-448542 aligncenter\" src=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/Stranger-Things-Hopper-700x300.jpg\" alt=\"Stranger Things 2 detail\" width=\"700\" height=\"300\" srcset=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/Stranger-Things-Hopper.jpg 700w, https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/Stranger-Things-Hopper-360x154.jpg 360w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 700px) 100vw, 700px\" /></p>\n<h2>A Long-Held Secret</h2>\n<p>In addition to whatever secrets are hinted at in those boxes, we&#8217;ll apparently also be getting a major reveal about Hopper&#8217;s history. Harbour and series creators <strong>the Duffer Brothers</strong> apparently have known since the very first season released in 2016, and he&#8217;s thrilled to get a chance to share it.</p>\n<blockquote><p>&#8220;There&#8217;s one thing in it that plays very big in this season that I&#8217;ve known since the first frame of the first season. Me and the Duffers would sit around and speculate, &#8216;Oh, wouldn&#8217;t this be cool?&#8217; the minute we started shooting. We never thought we&#8217;d even get a second season, and then we get to do it in this season. It&#8217;s so satisfying to have had an idea five years prior, and to go like, &#8216;Oh, this is a season when we&#8217;re gonna let out this secret that we were using just as a subtle thing to inform something.&#8217; We&#8217;re gonna lay it out finally, and it&#8217;s really cool.&#8221;</p></blockquote>\n<p>To find out Hopper&#8217;s big secret, you&#8217;ll have to watch season 4 of <em>Stranger Things. </em>Netflix has not announced a release date yet, but you can always watch seasons 1-3 again to try and figure out exactly what he&#8217;s going on about. Good luck!</p>\n<p>The post <a rel=\"nofollow\" href=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/stranger-things-season-4-hopper-secret/\">&#8216;Stranger Things&#8217; Season 4 Will Reveal a &#8220;Very Big&#8221; 02:35:16","updatedTime":"2021-07-13 02:35:16","title":"‘Memoria’ Trailer: Tilda Swinton Experiences a Mysterious Sensory Syndrome in the New Film From Apichatpong Weerasethakul","link":"https://www.slashfilm.com/?p=682790","description":"<p><a href=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/Memoria-Trailer.jpg\"><img class=\"aligncenter size-medium wp-image-682820\" src=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/Memoria-Trailer-700x321.jpg\" alt=\"Memoria Trailer \" width=\"700\" height=\"321\" srcset=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/Memoria-Trailer-700x321.jpg 700w, https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/Memoria-Trailer-360x165.jpg 360w, https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/Memoria-Trailer-768x352.jpg 768w, https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/Memoria-Trailer.jpg 948w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 700px) 100vw, 700px\" /></a></p>\n<p><strong>Apichatpong Weerasethakul</strong>, the acclaimed Thai filmmaker behind <em>Uncle Boonmee Who Can Recall His Past Lives</em>, <em>Cemetery of Splendour</em>, and more, is back with <strong><em>Memoria</em></strong>. The movie is set to premiere at the Cannes Film Festival, and we now have a mysterious, intriguing trailer that&#8217;s bound to make this shoot up to the top of your &#8220;must-see&#8221; list (if it wasn&#8217;t already there to begin with). <em>Memoria</em> follows a woman (<strong>Tilda Swinton</strong>) who &#8220;begins experiencing a mysterious sensory syndrome.&#8221;</p>\n<p><span id=\"more-682790\"></span></p>\n<h2><strong>Memoria Trailer </strong></h2>\n<p><iframe width=\"740\" height=\"416\" src=\"https://www.youtube.com/embed/PDU6B93ltds?feature=oembed\" frameborder=\"0\" allow=\"accelerometer; autoplay; clipboard-write; encrypted-media; gyroscope; picture-in-picture\" allowfullscreen></iframe></p>\n<p>God damn, now <em>this</em> is how you cut a trailer. &#8220;It&#8217;s like&#8230;a rumble, from the core of the Earth,&#8221; Tilda Swinton says as this trailer begins. &#8220;And then it shrinks.&#8221; What&#8217;s she talking about? The trailer doesn&#8217;t give you any real answers, and that&#8217;s what makes it so effective. So many movie trailers these days give the entire movie away, and that can be frustrating. So when a trailer like this comes along – a trailer that has absolutely no answers and only gets more and more mystifying as it unfolds – I get excited.</p>\n<p>The official synopsis describes <em>Memoria</em> as &#8220;a bewildering drama about a Scottish woman, who, after hearing a loud ‘bang’ at daybreak, begins experiencing a mysterious sensory syndrome while traversing the jungles of Colombia.&#8221;</p>\n<p>In addition to Swinton, the cast includes <strong>Jeanne Balibar</strong>, <strong>Daniel Giménez Cacho</strong>, <strong>Juan Pablo Urrego</strong>, and <strong>Elkin Diaz</strong>. <em>Memoria</em> will have its world premiere at the Cannes Film Festival on <strong>July 15</strong>, and we&#8217;ll hopefully learn when the rest of us can see it soon after.</p>\n<p><a href=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/memoria-poster.jpg\"><img class=\"aligncenter size-medium wp-image-682816\" src=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/memoria-poster-700x321.jpg\" alt=\"\" width=\"700\" height=\"321\" srcset=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/memoria-poster-700x321.jpg 700w, https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/memoria-poster-360x165.jpg 360w, https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/memoria-poster-768x352.jpg 768w, https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/memoria-poster.jpg 948w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 700px) 100vw, 700px\" /></a></p>\n<h2><strong>Expressions and Memories</strong></h2>\n<p>While all of this is very vague and mysterious, Apichatpong Weerasethakul&#8217;s director&#8217;s statement may shed some light on what&#8217;s going on here. Then again, it might not.</p>\n<p>&#8220;As a kid I was drawn to jungles, animals, and mountains,&#8221; the filmmaker said. &#8220;During the 70s, I grew up reading novels about hunters looking for treasures from lost civilizations. However, Thailand does not possess ancient empires full of gold, nor headhunter tribes, nor anacondas. Forty years later, I am still drawn to such landscapes but they are covered now with layers of other stories. I am attracted to the history of Latin America as if it was a missing part of my youth. I have come to Colombia to collect expressions and memories, not the Amazonian gold. I am deeply in debt to the individuals I have met in various cities, from psychologists, archaeologists, engineers, activists, to junk collectors.&#8221;</p>\n<p>The director then added:</p>\n<blockquote><p>&#8220;Another important factor in the birth of this project is my own hallucination. While researching, I often heard a loud noise at dawn. It was internal and has occurred in many of the places I visited. This symptom is inseparable from my exposure to Colombia. It has formed the basis of a character whose audio experience synchronizes with the country’s memory. I imagine the mountains here as an expression of people’s remembrances through centuries. The massive sierras, with their creases and creeks, are like the folds of the brain, or the curves of sound waves. With the scores of acts of violence and trauma, the terrain inflates and trembles, to become a country with never-ending landslides and earthquakes. The film itself is also seeking for a balance in this active topography. Its skeletons, the images and sounds, are shaken out of place. Perhaps this is a &#8216;sweet spot&#8217; where I and this film can synchronize, a state where delusion is the norm.&#8221;</p></blockquote>\n<p>The post <a rel=\"nofollow\" href=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/memoria-trailer/\">&#8216;Memoria&#8217; Trailer: Tilda Swinton Experiences a Mysterious Sensory Syndrome in the New Film From Apichatpong Weerasethakul</a> appeared Evangelista","articleImgCdnMap":{"https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/Memoria-Trailer-700x321.jpg":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx23/cdn3@2020_4/2021/07/12/18-35-25-435_202e10589d21a131.webp","https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/memoria-poster-700x321.jpg":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx3/cdn18@2020_4/2021/07/12/18-35-38-809_b5f1370576192aa6.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/slashfilm?d=yIl2AUoC8zA":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx/cdn75@2020_4/2021/07/12/18-35-39-281_9a442e8760d02cd4.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/slashfilm?i=lnb180JwNN4:i7ly-4fYoBU:V_sGLiPBpWU":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx30/cdn89@2020_1/2021/07/12/18-35-38-802_e39afe54eb7f0f50.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/slashfilm?d=I9og5sOYxJI":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx15/cdn20@2020_1/2021/07/12/18-35-39-646_879c5505f034c3d2.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/slashfilm?i=lnb180JwNN4:i7ly-4fYoBU:EGzC5_Ws_ZE":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx1/cdn75@2020_6/2021/07/12/18-35-38-807_23e27a6a92cc114f.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~r/slashfilm/~4/lnb180JwNN4":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx8/cdn92@2020_6/2021/07/12/18-35-38-818_5d86ece173cea1f5.webp"},"publishedOrCreatedDate":1626114916157},{"createdTime":"2021-07-13 02:35:16","updatedTime":"2021-07-13 02:35:16","title":"‘Loki’ Episode 5 Featured a Secret Chris Hemsworth Cameo","link":"https://www.slashfilm.com/?p=682443","description":"<p><img class=\"size-medium wp-image-682768 aligncenter\" src=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/thorragnarok-chrishemsworth-snakestory-700x300.jpg\" alt=\"Thor Ragnarok - Chris Hemsworth\" width=\"700\" height=\"300\" srcset=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/thorragnarok-chrishemsworth-snakestory.jpg 700w, https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/thorragnarok-chrishemsworth-snakestory-360x154.jpg 360w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 700px) 100vw, 700px\" /></p>\n<p>Last week&#8217;s fifth episode of Marvel&#8217;s <strong><em>Loki</em></strong> series on Disney+ <a href=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/loki-episode-5-easter-eggs/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">featured a ton of Easter eggs</a>, comic references, and callbacks to both Marvel Comics and the Marvel Cinematic Universe. In fact, we&#8217;ve just learned that one of the episode&#8217;s best Easter eggs actually contained another Easter egg that will make MCU fans very happy, and it involves <strong><em>Thor</em></strong> franchise star <strong>Chris Hemsworth</strong>.<span id=\"more-682443\"></span></p>\n<p>In the &#8220;<a href=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/loki-episode-5-review/\">Journey into Mystery</a>&#8221; episode of <em>Loki</em>, after our titular anti-hero is pruned by the Time Variance Authority, he finds himself in a desolate world called The Void. In this world, there are several other variations of Loki to welcome him, including <strong>Richard E. Grant</strong> as Classic Loki, <strong>Jack Veal</strong> as Kid Loki, <span class=\"Eq0J8 LrzXr kno-fv\"><strong>DeObia Oparei</strong> as Boastful Loki, and a bunch of pixels as Alligator Loki. The three Gods of Mischief take <strong>Tom Hiddleston</strong> as Loki Prime back to their lair. But before going inside, there was a little Easter egg lingering outside the lair.</span></p>\n<p>Among a bunch of debris in The Void, including school lunch trays and Thor&#8217;s hammer Mjolnir, there was a jar labeled T-365 featuring Frog Thor, an amphibian version of the God of Thunder also known as Throg. The little guy could be seen trying to break free of his container, screaming and making a big leap into the glass in an attempt to break it. The voice of that tiny amphibious Thor was none other than Chris Hemsworth himself.</p>\n<p><img class=\"size-medium wp-image-681405 aligncenter\" src=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/loki-frogthor-jar-700x300.jpg\" alt=\"Loki Episode 5\" width=\"700\" height=\"300\" srcset=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/loki-frogthor-jar.jpg 700w, https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/loki-frogthor-jar-360x154.jpg 360w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 700px) 100vw, 700px\" /></p>\n<h2>Secret Chris Hemsworth Cameo in Loki</h2>\n<p><em>Loki</em> director <strong>Kate Herron</strong> recently appear on <a class=\"external-link\" title=\"(opens new window)\" href=\"https://twitter.com/ForAllNerds/status/1413894361981624326\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\" aria-describedby=\"external-disclaimer\">For All Nerds</a> (via <a href=\"https://ew.com/tv/chris-hemsworth-cameo-loki-frog-thor/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Entertainment Weekly</a>), and the filmmaker revealed that Chris Hemsworth was recorded as the voice of Frog Thor. Herron said:</p>\n<blockquote><p>&#8220;We recorded Chris Hemsworth for that, by the way. We recorded him for that. His voice going &#8216;Ahhh!&#8217; That&#8217;s a whole new recording. Not recycled. He recorded that.&#8221;</p></blockquote>\n<p>It would have been easy to just grab an audio file from any of the previous <em>Thor</em> or <em>Avengers</em> movies and manipulate it to sound like tiny Frog Thor. But Herron likely didn&#8217;t have Hemsworth record just this scream. More than likely Hemsworth was brought in to record lines back when the plan was for Frog Thor to have a bigger appearance in the show&#8217;s first episode.</p>\n<p>As we recently learned, Frog Thor was <a href=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/loki-frog-thor-deleted-scene-details/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">originally intended to debut</a> in the Marvel Cinematic Universe during the Time Theater sequence from the show&#8217;s premiere. One of the clips played for Loki during his interrogation by Mobius would have seen Frog Thor beating up the God of Mischief as one of his more humiliating moments. That&#8217;s likely why Chris Hemsworth was brought in to record dialogue for the character, because having the actor brought in only to scream one time doesn&#8217;t seem like it&#8217;s worth the trouble.</p>\n<p>We&#8217;re hoping that we&#8217;ll get to see that deleted scene sometime down the road. At the very least, maybe there will be footage of Chris Hemsworth recording this dialogue in the <em>Loki</em> edition of the making-of documentary series <em>Assembled</em>, which will likely be arriving next week after the show&#8217;s finale airs this Wednesday.</p>\n<p>Catch up with the first five episodes of <em>Loki</em> over on Disney+ right now.</p>\n<p>The post <a rel=\"nofollow\" 02:35:16","updatedTime":"2021-07-13 02:35:16","title":"The Daily Stream: ‘Mona Lisa’ Features Another Killer Performance From Bob Hoskins","link":"https://www.slashfilm.com/?p=682212","description":"<p><img class=\"alignnone size-medium wp-image-682329 aligncenter\" src=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/Mona-Lisa-Bob-Hoskins-700x300.jpg\" alt=\"\" width=\"700\" height=\"300\" srcset=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/Mona-Lisa-Bob-Hoskins.jpg 700w, https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/Mona-Lisa-Bob-Hoskins-360x154.jpg 360w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 700px) 100vw, 700px\" /></p>\n<p><i data-stringify-type=\"italic\">(Welcome to </i><a href=\"https://slashfilm.com/tag/the-daily-stream\"><b data-stringify-type=\"bold\"><i data-stringify-type=\"italic\">T</i></b><b data-stringify-type=\"bold\"><i data-stringify-type=\"italic\">he Daily Stream</i></b></a><i data-stringify-type=\"italic\">, an ongoing series in which the /Film team shares what they&#8217;ve been watching, why it&#8217;s worth checking out, and where you can stream it.)</i></p>\n<p><strong>The Movie</strong>: <em>Mona Lisa<br />\n</em></p>\n<p><strong>Where You Can Stream It</strong>: HBO Max and The Criterion Channel</p>\n<p><strong>The Pitch: </strong>Bob Hoskins plays George, an uncouth ex-con who is given a job as a driver for a high-priced sex worker named Simone (Cathy Tyson). Though the two initially bicker as their personality styles clash, George finds himself slowly falling for Simone and pulled into London&#8217;s seedy underground on a quest to find one of her old friends who has gone missing.<strong><br />\n</strong></p>\n<p><strong>Why It&#8217;s Essential Viewing</strong>: Two words: Bob Hoskins. I grew up watching Hoskins as the bumbling pirate sidekick Smee in <em>Hook</em>, as Mario in <em>Super Mario Bros.</em>, and as the hardboiled detective Eddie Valiant in <em>Who Framed Roger Rabbit</em>. Throughout my childhood, those were the only three films I&#8217;d seen him in, and I was totally unaware that he had this whole other side to his career appearing in British crime movies. But now I&#8217;m making my way back through some of his filmography; he was terrific in <em>The Long Good Friday</em>, and I&#8217;m glad to have seen him in <em>Mona Lisa</em>, in which he earned an Academy Award nomination for his outstanding performance.<span id=\"more-682212\"></span></p>\n<p>Neil Jordan (<em>The Crying Game</em>, <em>Interview with a Vampire</em>) co-wrote and directed this neo-noir, which features some nice, contemplative, soulful moments from Hoskins and Tyson as they glide through the dirty, sleazy corners of the city and try to look respectable as Simone enters and exits fancy hotels to meet her clients. The camera is almost always at ground level, helping to ground us in George&#8217;s perspective as he tries to get to know his estranged daughter, gets embroiled in dangerous drama with his old boss (Michael Caine), and slowly falls harder and harder for Simone.</p>\n<p>It is a neo-noir, though, so it&#8217;s not all fun and games: people&#8217;s motivations and true feelings are eventually exposed, and the way Hoskins acts and reacts to these plot twists makes me wish I&#8217;d sought out his work in the gangster genre years ago.</p>\n<p><img class=\"alignnone size-medium wp-image-682316 aligncenter\" src=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/Plastic-Spaghetti-700x300.jpg\" alt=\"\" width=\"700\" height=\"300\" srcset=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/Plastic-Spaghetti.jpg 700w, https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/Plastic-Spaghetti-360x154.jpg 360w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 700px) 100vw, 700px\" /></p>\n<p>One of my favorite things about the movie is George&#8217;s friendship with his best pal Thomas, played by Robbie Coltrane. The two of them bring a sense of warm history to their relationship, but the best part is that the film devotes time to showing us Thomas&#8217;s off-the-wall job, which seems to be making bizarre pieces of art. At one point, the camera pans across Thomas&#8217;s warehouse apartment/work studio to reveal that he has made multiple plates of fake spaghetti. After being told that the spaghetti is &#8220;ornamental,&#8221; George asks Thomas where he got it. &#8220;Contacts, George,&#8221; Thomas replies. &#8220;Can&#8217;t find plastic spaghetti just anywhere.&#8221; That level of weird specificity is sorely lacking from many films that are made today, and I encourage filmmakers (and studios and people in power) to do more stuff like this that doesn&#8217;t contribute to pushing the plot forward.</p>\n<p>The post <a rel=\"nofollow\" href=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/the-daily-stream-mona-lisa/\">The Daily Stream: &#8216;Mona Lisa&#8217; Features Another Killer Performance From Bob Hoskins</a> appeared first on <a rel=\"nofollow\" href=\"https://www.slashfilm.com\">/Film</a>.</p>\n<div class=\"feedflare\">\n<a 02:35:16","updatedTime":"2021-07-13 02:35:16","title":"‘Black Widow’ Smashes Pandemic Box Office Records With the Biggest Opening Since ‘Star Wars: The Rise of Skywalker’","link":"https://www.slashfilm.com/?p=682421","description":"<p><img class=\"aligncenter wp-image-679128 size-medium\" src=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/BBU-32704_R3-e1624823397940-700x299.jpg\" alt=\"black widow box office\" width=\"700\" height=\"299\" srcset=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/BBU-32704_R3-e1624823397940-700x300.jpg 700w, https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/BBU-32704_R3-e1624823397940-360x154.jpg 360w, https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/BBU-32704_R3-e1624823397940-768x328.jpg 768w, https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/BBU-32704_R3-e1624823397940.jpg 1500w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 700px) 100vw, 700px\" /></p>\n<p>Consider <em><strong>Black Widow</strong></em> a win for the pandemic box office, movie theaters, and (possibly) some sort of studio transparency in the Wild West of this new streaming age. After countless delays and shifting release dates, the latest installment in the Marvel Cinematic Universe finally swung into theaters this weekend and fully stuck the landing in that trademark Natasha Romanoff superhero pose.</p>\n<p><span id=\"more-682421\"></span></p>\n<p><a href=\"https://variety.com/2021/film/box-office/marvel-black-widow-box-office-opening-weekend-1235016977/\">Variety</a> has the numbers to prove that nothing, not even a pandemic, is a match for the MCU. Director <strong>Cate Shortland&#8217;s</strong> <em>Black Widow</em>, starring <strong>Scarlett Johansson</strong> and <strong>Florence Pugh</strong>, hauled in $80 million this weekend, <a href=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/f9-box-office-opening-weekend/\">supplanting last week&#8217;s <em><strong>F9</strong></em> performance</a> and vaulting Marvel&#8217;s action flick to the top of the charts in the second consecutive weekend featuring a movie setting a new pandemic record. It&#8217;s the largest domestic opening since Disney/Lucasfilm&#8217;s<em> Star Wars: The Rise of Skywalker</em> <a href=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/star-wars-the-rise-of-skywalker-box-office-cats/\">opened in December 2019</a>.</p>\n<p>If you&#8217;re curious about a comparison to the Before Times, <em><strong>Spider-Man: Far From Home</strong></em> was the MCU&#8217;s previous theatrical release in 2019 and opened to a staggering $185 million debut. And also for comparison&#8217;s sake, <em><strong>Captain Marvel</strong></em> dropped that same year as well to the opening weekend tune of $153 million.</p>\n<p>Obviously, the pandemic has completely upended our expectations and standards for releases these days, so <em>Black Widow&#8217;s</em> $80 million domestic and $158 worldwide are hardly anything to dismiss.</p>\n<p><img class=\"size-medium wp-image-608842 aligncenter\" src=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/disney-plus-india-700x321.jpg\" alt=\"disney plus india\" width=\"700\" height=\"321\" srcset=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/disney-plus-india-700x321.jpg 700w, https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/disney-plus-india-360x165.jpg 360w, https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/disney-plus-india-768x352.jpg 768w, https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/disney-plus-india.jpg 948w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 700px) 100vw, 700px\" /></p>\n<h2>The Disney+ Wrinkle</h2>\n<p>Of course, the pandemic has also forced studios to adapt with the times. At the behest of AT&#38;T, Warner Bros. (in)famously shook up the industry by announcing its plan to release its catalogue of films both in theaters and on streaming service HBO Max simultaneously. In a similarly unexpected change from the standard operating procedure thus far, Disney has finally released numbers for <em>Black Widow&#8217;s</em> Premier Access charge on Disney+ and combined them with the total weekend tally to paint a slightly more optimistic picture. In a notable deviation from box office numbers (which studios split with theaters), Disney gets to keep 100% of its Disney+ profits.</p>\n<p>Touting these numbers as &#8220;consumer spend globally&#8221;, a hilariously corporate term that just rolls off the tongue, <em>Black Widow</em> apparently gained an additional $60 million through Disney+ rentals which are currently set at $30 a pop. Many in the industry consider <a href=\"https://www.forbes.com/sites/scottmendelson/2021/07/11/black-widow-box-office-scarlett-johansson-florence-pugh-marvel-disney-plus/?utm_source=pocket_mylist&#38;sh=5760c4702d6c\">this number-pushing as gamesmanship</a>, allowing Disney to claim a larger piece of the box office pie for PR purposes while the rest of us are left to take the studio at their word. It&#8217;s worth noting that <em>Black Widow</em> likely would&#8217;ve made more without making Premier Access an option, which allows families of three or more to save considerable money that otherwise would&#8217;ve gone to ticket sales (and concessions, which tend to be the livelihood for theaters). It remains to be seen how Disney adjusts for their next theatrical release, <em><strong>Shang-Chi and the Legend of the Ten Rings</strong></em>, and whether Premier Access will continue to be a part of their plan.</p>\n<p>As for the rest of the box office, <em>F9</em> came in at second place with a total of $10.8 million, a precipitous drop from its opening weekend numbers but good enough for a worldwide total of $541.8 million. Universal also claims the third and fourth-place spots with <em><strong>Boss Baby: Family Business</strong></em>, at $8.7 million, and <em><strong>The Forever Purge</strong></em> with an addition $6.7 million. <em><strong>A Quiet Place Part II</strong></em>, meanwhile, rounds out the top 5 with another $3 million.</p>\n<p>The post <a rel=\"nofollow\" href=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/black-widow-box-office-pandemic-record/\">&#8216;Black Widow&#8217; Smashes Pandemic Box Office Records With the Biggest Opening Since &#8216;Star Wars: The Rise of Skywalker&#8217;</a> appeared first on <a rel=\"nofollow\" href=\"https://www.slashfilm.com\">/Film</a>.</p>\n<div class=\"feedflare\">\n<a Watch it below.</p>\n<p><span id=\"more-682179\"></span></p>\n<h2><strong>Almost Famous Deleted Scene</strong></h2>\n<p><iframe width=\"740\" height=\"416\" src=\"https://www.youtube.com/embed/hq7QCVxakWs?feature=oembed\" frameborder=\"0\" allow=\"accelerometer; autoplay; clipboard-write; encrypted-media; gyroscope; picture-in-picture\" allowfullscreen></iframe></p>\n<p><em>Almost Famous</em> turns 21 this year, and I&#8217;ll give you a minute to stop and reflect on that, and on how old you&#8217;ve become. I think it&#8217;s safe to say this is Cameron Crowe&#8217;s most-loved movie (although I personally prefer <em>Vanilla Sky</em>), and the flick is coming to 4K on <strong>July 13, 2021</strong>. That coincides with the release of a limited-edition Uber Box set.</p>\n<p>&#8220;We are extremely proud to revisit <em>Almost Famous </em>with a very special bounty of goodness,&#8221; said Cameron Crowe. &#8220;For the first time, we’ve created a Deluxe Soundtrack that features nearly every song from the film, along with Nancy Wilson&#8217;s wonderfully evocative score. We&#8217;re also thrilled to finally preserve both versions of the film, along with a collection of rare new bonus features, on these beautiful new 4K and Blu-ray releases as part of Paramount Presents. Long live physical media!&#8221;</p>\n<p>The 4K release has been remastered in 4K Ultra HD with Dolby Vision and HDR-10 for ultra-vivid picture quality. The limited-edition 4K Ultra HD Steelbook includes both the original theatrical cut (plus access to a digital copy) and the Bootleg cut, along with new bonus content &#8220;offering a backstage pass into the creative process through a new interview with Crowe, extended scenes, rock-school sessions, a look at the casting and costumes, and more.&#8221;</p>\n<p><em>Almost Famous</em> is the &#8220;semi-autobiographical odyssey of 15-year-old William Miller (<strong>Patrick Fugit</strong>), whose writing talent and earnest passion for rock music earns him an assignment for Rolling Stone, interviewing and touring with Stillwater (<strong>Billy Crudup</strong>, <strong>Jason Lee</strong>). Penny Lane (<strong>Kate Hudson</strong>) is the young groupie who guides him through the wild world of rock heroes, all-night parties, and the most dangerous experience of all—love.&#8221;</p>\n<p><a href=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/almost-famous-musical.jpg\"><img class=\"aligncenter size-medium wp-image-552042\" 700px\" /></a></p>\n<h2><strong>4K Special Features</strong></h2>\n<p>Here&#8217;s all the neat stuff that comes with the new release, with some special features ported over from previous 4K, there&#8217;s also a big box set that compiles the various versions of the film&#8217;s soundtracks. The set &#8220;encompasses an expanded soundtrack with five CDs, seven 180-gram black vinyl discs, and a brand new 7-inch for Stillwater’s “Fever Dog.” The expanded soundtrack includes songs from The Beach Boys, Joni Mitchell, Led Zeppelin, Neil Young &#38; Crazy Horse, The Who, and Yes, plus all the songs created for the film’s fictional aspiring rock group Stillwater, most written for the movie by Cameron Crowe, Heart’s Nancy Wilson and Grammy Award-winning guitarist, Peter Frampton.&#8221;</p>\n<p>The set also includes &#8220;<span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">a 40-page photo book and memoir housed in a film-prop-replica of William Miller’s high-school notebook; the first-ever complete William Miller cover story on Stillwater as a 1973 </span><i><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">Rolling Stone</span></i><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\"> newsprint; two replica ticket stubs; and a Stillwater tour poster. Exclusively available only in the Uber Boxset is a Stillwater Cleveland concert poster and a backstage poster; six film-prop-replica backstage passes (some seen throughout the film); three film-prop-replica business cards for Dick Roswell (Stillwater road manager), Lester Bangs (</span><i><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">Creem</span></i><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\"> magazine), and Ben Fong-Torres (</span><i><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">Rolling Stone</span></i><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\"> magazine); and three photo prints of cast members. Along with the thirteen-disc Uber Deluxe box, Universal is issuing two six-LP editions—one on black vinyl, the other with colored vinyl discs; a five-CD Super Deluxe set including 102 tracks, 36 of them previously unreleased songs; a separate 12-inch vinyl EP with all 6 of Stillwater’s songs; a Record Store Day exclusive with the 7 original demos of the Stillwater songs, five performed by Wilson the other two by Frampton; a two-LP vinyl version of the original soundtrack album; a two-CD Deluxe Edition of the original soundtrack.&#8221; </span></p>\n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">Yeah, href=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/west-side-story-release-date-and-more.jpg\"><img class=\"aligncenter size-medium wp-image-682876\" More</strong>, our no-frills, zero B.S. guide to when and where you can watch upcoming movies and shows, and everything else you could possibly stand to know.)</em></p>\n<p><strong>Steven Spielberg</strong> finally gets to make a musical with <strong><em>West Side Story</em></strong>, a new adaptation of the 1957 Broadway musical by Arthur Laurents, Leonard Bernstein, and Stephen Sondheim. <em>West Side Story</em> will arrive this December, but for now, here&#8217;s everything you need to know about the movie in advance, including the release date, cast and crew, and more.</p>\n<p><span id=\"more-682785\"></span></p>\n<h2><strong>West Side Story Release Date and Where You Can Watch It</strong></h2>\n<p><em>West Side Story</em> is headed to theaters on <strong>December 10, 2021</strong>. It was originally due out last December, but the pandemic got in the way. Appropriately enough, delaying the release by one year will have this <em>West Side Story</em> arriving to coincide with the 60th anniversary of the release of the original 1961 film. As of now, <em>West Side Story</em> will be exclusive to theaters.</p>\n<h2><strong>What is West Side Story</strong><strong>?</strong></h2>\n<p><em>West Side Story</em> is an adaptation of the 1957 Broadway musical with a book by Arthur Laurents, music by Leonard Bernstein, and lyrics by Stephen Sondheim, loosely inspired by <em>Romeo and Juliet</em>. The musical was previously adapted to film in 1961. That adaptation remains widely acclaimed, and was nominated for 11 Academy Awards and won 10, including Best Picture – which means it&#8217;s a tough act for Steven Spielberg to follow. But since he&#8217;s one of our best living directors, he&#8217;ll probably be fine. One key difference between this adaptation and the 1961 film is that Spielberg pushed to make sure performers with Hispanic backgrounds played Hispanic characters, and, per <a href=\"https://www.vanityfair.com/hollywood/2020/03/a-first-look-at-steven-spielbergs-west-side-story\">Vanity Fair</a>, the filmmaker &#8220;estimates that 20 of the 33 Puerto Rican characters are specifically Puerto Rican or of Puerto Rican descent.&#8221;</p>\n<p>“They brought themselves, and everything they believe and everything about them—they brought that to the work,&#8221; Spielberg said. &#8220;And there was so much interaction between the cast wanting to be able to commit to the Puerto Rican experience. They all represent, I think, a diversity, both within the Puerto Rican, Nuyorican community as well as the broader Latinx community. And they took that seriously.&#8221;</p>\n<h2><strong>West Side Story Synopsis</strong></h2>\n<p><em>West Side Story</em> &#8220;tells the classic tale of fierce rivalries and young love in 1957 New York City.&#8221; The young lovers are Tony and Maria, who fall for each other despite having connections to feuding street gangs The Jets and The Sharks. Maria <a href=\"https://www.vanityfair.com/hollywood/2020/03/a-first-look-at-steven-spielbergs-west-side-story\">is</a> &#8220;part of the wave of Puerto Rican migrants who traded one island for another when they came to New York seeking a new life in the post–World War II economic boom. Her streetwise Casanova is Tony&#8230;who once led a gang of local toughs known as the Jets, but has since outgrown them. Tony’s old friends are engaged in an escalating battle for control of the neighborhood against Puerto Rican rivals who call themselves the Sharks, led by Maria’s brother Bernardo.&#8221;</p>\n<h2><strong>West Side Story Director, Crew, and More</strong></h2>\n<p><em>West Side Story</em> is directed by a young up-and-comer named <strong>Steven Spielberg</strong>. That kid&#8217;s going places, let me tell you. <strong>Tony Kushner</strong>, who has worked with Spielberg on <em>Munich</em> and <em>Lincoln</em>, wrote the script. Kushner is also an executive producer. <strong>Justin Peck </strong>choreographed the musical numbers in the film while Los Angeles Philharmonic conductor <strong>Gustavo Dudamel</strong> handled the recording of the score, which was arranged by composer and conductor <strong>David Newman</strong>. <strong>Jeanine Tesori</strong> supervised the cast on vocals while <strong>Matt Sullivan</strong> served as executive music producer for the film. Spielberg produces along with <strong>Kristie Macosko Krieger</strong> and<strong> Kevin McCollum</strong>.</p>\n<h2><strong>West Side Story Cast</strong></h2>\n<p><em>West Side Story</em> stars <strong>Ansel Elgort</strong>* as Tony; <strong>Rachel Zegler</strong> as Maria; <strong>Ariana DeBose</strong> as Anita; <strong>David Alvarez</strong> as Bernardo;<strong> Mike Faist</strong> as Riff; <strong>Josh Andrés Rivera</strong> as Chino; <strong>Ana Isabelle</strong> as Rosalía; <strong>Corey Stoll</strong> as Lieutenant Schrank; <strong>Brian d&#8217;Arcy Jame</strong>s as Officer Krupke; and <strong>Rita Moreno</strong>, who won an Oscar for playing Anita in the 1961 movie, as Valentina, who owns the corner store in which Tony works.</p>\n<p>*It&#8217;s worth noting that in 2020, a woman accused Elgort of sexual misconduct in 2014 when she was 17 and he was 20. Elgort <a href=\"https://www.newsweek.com/ansel-elgort-says-relationship-accuser-was-consensual-not-assault-1512368\">denied</a> the allegation and said the relationship was brief and consensual. Since then there&#8217;s been next to no coverage of the story, but that might change the closer the film gets to release.</p>\n<h2><strong>West Side Story Trailer</strong></h2>\n<p><iframe width=\"740\" height=\"416\" src=\"https://www.youtube.com/embed/CbUM27qw6a8?feature=oembed\" frameborder=\"0\" allow=\"accelerometer; autoplay; clipboard-write; encrypted-media; gyroscope; picture-in-picture\" allowfullscreen></iframe></p>\n<p>The post <a rel=\"nofollow\" href=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/west-side-story-release-date/\">West Side Story: Release Date, Cast and More</a> Again","link":"https://www.slashfilm.com/?p=682796","description":"<p><img class=\"aligncenter wp-image-679952 size-medium\" https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/Escape-Room-Tournament-of-Champions-Release-Date-768x352.jpg 768w, https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/Escape-Room-Tournament-of-Champions-Release-Date.jpg 948w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 700px) 100vw, 700px\" /></p>\n<p>Escape rooms are making a comeback— and they&#8217;re even more life-threatening than you remember!</p>\n<p>A sequel to 2019’s <em><strong>Escape Room</strong></em> is coming to theaters later this month, once again gathering a group of strangers and forcing them to work their way through a series of deadly puzzles. The first movie was especially lethal, leaving only two survivors in its wake, but <em><strong>Escape Room: Tournament of Champions</strong></em> is going for the gold. Based on the latest clip, the rooms have become even more dangerous and complex.</p>\n<p>Check out the newest clip from <em>Escape Room: Tournament of Champions </em>below.</p>\n<p><span id=\"more-682796\"></span></p>\n<h2>Escape Room Tournament of Champions Clip</h2>\n<p><iframe width=\"740\" height=\"416\" src=\"https://www.youtube.com/embed/UFpNXcsMK1E?feature=oembed\" frameborder=\"0\" allow=\"accelerometer; autoplay; clipboard-write; encrypted-media; gyroscope; picture-in-picture\" allowfullscreen></iframe></p>\n<p>You might have noticed that <em>Escape Room: Tournament of Champions</em> features a couple of familiar faces. Returners Zoey Davis (<strong>Taylor Russell</strong>) and Ben Miller (<strong>Logan Mille</strong>r) managed to survive each of the puzzles from <em>Escape Room</em> and have the misfortunate of being caught up once again. Luckily, they aren&#8217;t alone, and their newest companions are already familiar with the deadly puzzle rooms. The villainous corporation Minos Escape Rooms has found a way to gather its survivors in an intense tournament of past champions.</p>\n<p>As we see in the clip, these puzzles promise to be much more difficult than the first. This time around, they weren&#8217;t designed for amateurs but for the very best of the deadly escape room niche. But even if all of these people have survived Minos once before, who&#8217;s to say if they can do it again?</p>\n<p>At the very least, they’re much better suited than the last movies group: they begin the bank room by springing into action, pairing off, and searching for clues. We can expect less of their initial panic since they&#8217;re already so familiar with what&#8217;s at stake. The champions remember these <em><strong>Saw</strong></em>-like circumstances like the back of their hands because they’ve already lived them once before.</p>\n<p>Wasting no time, they each talk through the riddle, connecting the blank bills to the words repeated over the loudspeaker. In a matter of seconds, they realize the bills must be soaked in blood – and just as things start coming together, the Game Master ramps up the stakes. Lasers erupt from all angles of the room and both Zoey and a newcomer fall back into them. But it looks like we won’t be getting answers on who survives until the movie&#8217;s debut in theaters.</p>\n<p><img class=\"aligncenter size-medium wp-image-515260\" src=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/escape-room-700x291.jpg\" alt=\"escape room trailer\" width=\"700\" height=\"291\" srcset=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/escape-room-700x291.jpg 700w, https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/escape-room-360x150.jpg 360w, https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/escape-room-768x319.jpg 768w, https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/escape-room.jpg 1440w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 700px) 100vw, 700px\" /></p>\n<h2>A Promising Follow-Up</h2>\n<p>The first <em>Escape Room</em> was a delightful surprise. It was nothing like we haven&#8217;t seen before, a wild amalgamation of <em>Saw</em>, <em>Final Destination</em>, and the much more PG <em>Maze Runner</em>. <strong>Adam Robitel</strong>&#8216;s <em>Escape Room</em> movies are fun with puzzles that are largely life-threatening and occasionally traumatizing. They promise everything from giant ovens and upside-down billiards to hospital rooms filling with poisonous gas and yes, a bank safe filled with lasers.</p>\n<p>The first <em>Escape Room</em> <a href=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/escape-room-review/\">didn&#8217;t come together perfectly</a>, but it was still plenty of fun all the way through. Perhaps <em>Escape Room: Tournament of Champion</em>s has figured out how to marry 90 minutes of fun intrigue with its overly complicated ending concept. Either way, it looks like we can hope for more of the same, dialed up a few hundred notches.</p>\n<p><em>Escape Room: Tournament of Champions</em> releases in theaters on <strong>July 16, 2021</strong>.</p>\n<p>The post <a rel=\"nofollow\" href=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/escape-room-tournament-of-champions-clip/\">&#8216;Escape Room: Tournament of Champions&#8217; Clip: Escape Rooms Are Making A Deadly Comeback – Again</a> appeared first on <a rel=\"nofollow\" href=\"https://www.slashfilm.com\">/Film</a>.</p>\n<div class=\"feedflare\">\n<a href=\"http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/slashfilm?a=FwikmOsfCn8:UN35XsFX_E0:yIl2AUoC8zA\"><img src=\"http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/slashfilm?d=yIl2AUoC8zA\" border=\"0\"></img></a> <a Russell","articleImgCdnMap":{"https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/Escape-Room-Tournament-of-Champions-Release-Date-700x321.jpg":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx1/cdn63@2020_5/2021/07/12/18-35-16-429_a00eabdb5dd038f2.webp","https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/escape-room-700x291.jpg":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx6/cdn95@2020_1/2021/07/12/18-35-38-878_b3337fca49fd4d1a.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/slashfilm?d=yIl2AUoC8zA":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx/cdn75@2020_4/2021/07/12/18-35-39-281_9a442e8760d02cd4.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/slashfilm?i=FwikmOsfCn8:UN35XsFX_E0:V_sGLiPBpWU":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx5oss/cdn33@2020_1/2021/07/12/18-35-38-840_41bc37f40fcbb43e.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/slashfilm?d=I9og5sOYxJI":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx15/cdn20@2020_1/2021/07/12/18-35-39-646_879c5505f034c3d2.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/slashfilm?i=FwikmOsfCn8:UN35XsFX_E0:EGzC5_Ws_ZE":null,"http://feeds.feedburner.com/~r/slashfilm/~4/FwikmOsfCn8":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx21/cdn80@2020_1/2021/07/12/18-35-38-816_98e488a1ed99baa9.webp"},"publishedOrCreatedDate":1626114916155},{"createdTime":"2021-07-13 02:35:16","updatedTime":"2021-07-13 02:35:16","title":"Margot Robbie Doesn’t Know When She’ll Play Harley Quinn Again","link":"https://www.slashfilm.com/?p=682431","description":"<p><a href=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/More-Harley-Quinn-Movies.jpg\"><img class=\"aligncenter size-medium wp-image-682774\" src=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/More-Harley-Quinn-Movies-700x321.jpg\" alt=\"More Harley Quinn Movies\" width=\"700\" height=\"321\" srcset=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/More-Harley-Quinn-Movies-700x321.jpg 700w, https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/More-Harley-Quinn-Movies-360x165.jpg 360w, https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/More-Harley-Quinn-Movies-768x352.jpg 768w, https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/More-Harley-Quinn-Movies.jpg 948w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 700px) 100vw, 700px\" /></a></p>\n<p><strong>Margot Robbie</strong> reprises the role of Harley Quinn in the upcoming <strong><em>The Suicide Squad</em></strong>, but what happens after that? According to Robbie herself, she doesn&#8217;t know. For now, the actress says she needs a break from Harley. In a recent interview, Robbie revealed that she&#8217;s unsure of when we&#8217;ll see Harley again. On top of that, Robbie had no idea about her character&#8217;s fate mentioned in the needless epilogue from <strong><em>Zack Snyder&#8217;s Justice League</em></strong>.</p>\n<p><span id=\"more-682431\"></span></p>\n<p>After playing Harley Quinn three times on the big screen in <em>Suicide Squad</em>, <em>Birds of Prey</em>, and the upcoming <em>The Suicide Squad</em>, Margot Robbie needs a break. Speaking with <a href=\"https://ew.com/movies/margot-robbie-harley-quinn-the-suicide-squad/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Entertainment Weekly</a>, Robbie revealed her plans to take some time off from the DC character. &#8220;It was kind of back-to-back filming <em>Birds&#8230;</em> and filming this, so I was kind of like, oof, I need a break from Harley because she&#8217;s exhausting,&#8221; Robbie told EW. &#8220;I don&#8217;t know when we&#8217;re next going to see her. I&#8217;m just as intrigued as everyone else is.&#8221;</p>\n<p>Originally created by Paul Dini and Bruce Timm for <em>Batman: The Animated Series</em>, Harley Quinn quickly became something of a fan favorite, crossing over from the animated TV series into the DC comics. Robbie wasn&#8217;t the first actress to play the character in live-action – Mia Sara played the character in the short-lived live-action <em>Birds of Prey</em> TV series in 2002. But Robbie was the first to play Harley on the big screen, and the role suits her nicely. That said, fans of the character don&#8217;t have to worry about Harley up and vanishing. While Robbie may be taking a break after <em>The Suicide Squad</em>, Harley will live on in the <a href=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/harley-quinn-review-dc-universes-new-animated-series-is-funny-violent-and-very-r-rated/\">excellent <strong><em>Harley Quinn</em></strong> animated series</a>, where the character is voiced by <strong>Kaley Cuoco</strong>.</p>\n<p><a href=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/justice-league-we-live-in-a-society-scene.jpg\"><img class=\"aligncenter size-medium wp-image-665268\" src=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/justice-league-we-live-in-a-society-scene-700x321.jpg\" alt=\"justice league we live in a society scene\" width=\"700\" height=\"321\" srcset=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/justice-league-we-live-in-a-society-scene-700x321.jpg 700w, https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/justice-league-we-live-in-a-society-scene-360x165.jpg 360w, https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/justice-league-we-live-in-a-society-scene-768x352.jpg 768w, https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/justice-league-we-live-in-a-society-scene.jpg 948w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 700px) 100vw, 700px\" /></a></p>\n<h2><strong>We Live In a Society Where Margot Robbie Hasn&#8217;t Seen The Snyder Cut</strong></h2>\n<p><em>Zack Snyder&#8217;s Justice League</em>, AKA The Snyder Cut, ended up <a href=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/zack-snyders-justice-league-review/\">being much better</a> than I would&#8217;ve ever suspected. Don&#8217;t get me wrong – the film has its problems, but I appreciate the overall vision Snyder was going for – up to a point. That point is an utterly baffling epilogue where Batman has a nightmare set in a piss-colored future where Darkseid has taken over Earth and Superman is evil. In this seemingly endless scene, Batman and Joker get into an argument that truly underscores the awfulness of Jared Leto&#8217;s portrayal of the Clown Prince of Crime. And during this moment it&#8217;s revealed that Harley Quinn is dead – in fact, she died in Batman&#8217;s arms.</p>\n<p>But Margot Robbie doesn&#8217;t know anything about that. In the same EW interview, Robbie was made aware of this epilogue and Harley&#8217;s fate, to which she replied: &#8220;Whaaat? I didn&#8217;t know that. Thank you for telling me!&#8221; Robbie went on to add:</p>\n<blockquote><p>&#8220;The film version of the DC universe, I actually think they&#8217;re a lot like the comics. You pick up one comic and something&#8217;s happening and then you pick up the next comic and maybe that character&#8217;s not alive, maybe that character&#8217;s not with that person, maybe that character looks completely different. Each movie is its own sort of thing, and I think that works in the comic book world, and I think that works in the DC film world as well. It&#8217;s not like Marvel where everything is more obviously linked in a more linear way. It feels like there&#8217;s so many adjacent stories, worlds, and films happening at the same time, just like there are in the comics. So, yeah, I didn&#8217;t know that, but it doesn&#8217;t necessarily change what other people are able to do with this universe, I don&#8217;t think.&#8221;</p></blockquote>\n<p>To be fair, the <em>Justice League</em> epilogue is all a dream, and Snyder&#8217;s continuity isn&#8217;t the continuity that the DCEU is following, so there&#8217;s no real worry about Harley being dead in the movies. But Robbie has certainly earned a break from the character, and it&#8217;ll be interesting to see when (and if) she returns to the role.</p>\n<p><em>The Suicide Squad</em> opens on <strong>August 6, 2021</strong>.</p>\n<p>The post <a rel=\"nofollow\" href=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/more-harley-quinn-movies/\">Margot Robbie Doesn&#8217;t Know When She&#8217;ll Play Harley Quinn Again</a> appeared first on <a rel=\"nofollow\" href=\"https://www.slashfilm.com\">/Film</a>.</p>\n<div class=\"feedflare\">\n<a href=\"http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/slashfilm?a=v4xpuz5LQsk:kLPIWP6NWt0:yIl2AUoC8zA\"><img src=\"http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/slashfilm?d=yIl2AUoC8zA\" border=\"0\"></img></a> <a href=\"http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/slashfilm?a=v4xpuz5LQsk:kLPIWP6NWt0:V_sGLiPBpWU\"><img src=\"http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/slashfilm?i=v4xpuz5LQsk:kLPIWP6NWt0:V_sGLiPBpWU\" src=\"http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/slashfilm?i=v4xpuz5LQsk:kLPIWP6NWt0:EGzC5_Ws_ZE\" border=\"0\"></img></a>\n</div><img src=\"http://feeds.feedburner.com/~r/slashfilm/~4/v4xpuz5LQsk\" height=\"1\" width=\"1\" alt=\"\"/>","descriptionType":"html","publishedDate":"Mon, 12 Jul 2021 15:09:20 +0000","feedId":21,"bgimg":"https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/More-Harley-Quinn-Movies-700x321.jpg","linkMd5":"1bb48dd25af87477ecf3f92725cd38a5","bgimgJsdelivr":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx7/cdn56@2020_4/2021/07/12/18-35-37-380_7c9129e2e2772b8a.webp","destWidth":700,"destHeight":321,"sourceBytes":28159,"destBytes":16348,"author":"Chris Evangelista","articleImgCdnMap":{"https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/More-Harley-Quinn-Movies-700x321.jpg":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx7/cdn56@2020_4/2021/07/12/18-35-37-380_7c9129e2e2772b8a.webp","https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/justice-league-we-live-in-a-society-scene-700x321.jpg":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx19/cdn73@2020_6/2021/07/12/18-35-39-471_20cfd76cb3213123.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/slashfilm?d=yIl2AUoC8zA":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx/cdn75@2020_4/2021/07/12/18-35-39-281_9a442e8760d02cd4.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/slashfilm?i=v4xpuz5LQsk:kLPIWP6NWt0:V_sGLiPBpWU":null,"http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/slashfilm?d=I9og5sOYxJI":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx15/cdn20@2020_1/2021/07/12/18-35-39-646_879c5505f034c3d2.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/slashfilm?i=v4xpuz5LQsk:kLPIWP6NWt0:EGzC5_Ws_ZE":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx30/cdn9@2020_4/2021/07/12/18-35-39-539_13a93cfdefbfd086.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~r/slashfilm/~4/v4xpuz5LQsk":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx4/cdn51@2020_1/2021/07/12/18-35-39-134_d9421223fe7a6c0e.webp"},"publishedOrCreatedDate":1626114916164},{"createdTime":"2021-07-13 02:35:16","updatedTime":"2021-07-13 02:35:16","title":"‘The French Dispatch’ Review: Wes Anderson’s Whimsical New Masterwork is a Symphony of Excess [Cannes]","link":"https://www.slashfilm.com/?p=682899","description":"<p><img class=\"aligncenter size-medium wp-image-682904\" src=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/the-french-dispatch-e1626113681478-700x299.jpeg\" alt=\"the french dispatch review\" width=\"700\" height=\"299\" srcset=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/the-french-dispatch-e1626113681478-700x300.jpeg 700w, https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/the-french-dispatch-e1626113681478-360x154.jpeg 360w, https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/the-french-dispatch-e1626113681478-768x328.jpeg 768w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 700px) 100vw, 700px\" /></p>\n<p>Watching <strong>Wes Anderson</strong>’s <strong><em>The French Dispatch </em></strong>is a delirious experience. It’s akin to being a guest at some amazing meal, with each course more stunning than the last, and just as you wish to take in a moment to admire each dish, the crumbs are whisked away for a new treat to be delivered by nimble servers. It’s a film that weaponizes whimsy in ways that will dazzle die-hard fans of the director. As long as your heart is open, your ears attuned to the pace of the proceedings and eyes accustomed to this mode of staging, you’ll have a quite remarkable experience gorging on this gorgeous film.</p>\n<p><span id=\"more-682899\"></span></p>\n<p>Told through three primary storylines presented as articles ripped from the fictional literary magazine that gives the film its name, we meet many of the regular troupe that have made much of Anderson’s oeuvre such a wonderful ride over the last few decades. <strong>Bill Murray</strong>, <strong>Owen Wilson,</strong> <strong>Jason Schwartzman</strong>, <strong>Edward Norton</strong>, and <strong>Willem Dafoe</strong> are joined by likes of <strong>Liev Schreiber</strong>, <strong>Saoirse Ronan</strong>, <strong>Timothée Chalamet</strong>, <strong>Matheiu Amalric</strong>, <strong>Stephen Park</strong>, <strong>Lyna Khoudri</strong>, and <strong>Frances McDormand</strong>. Simply reveling in this cast list is enough to excite, and each perfectly inhabits their place within the cacophonous world of Ennui-sur-Blasé, a small town that wakes up quickly in the morning, and is the home to a magazine setup by a Kansas-based publisher as a kind of foreign outpost to bring stories of the continent back to local readers.</p>\n<p>Perhaps the most charming is the story of a prisoner artist, his muse, and the agent responsible for bringing to the world his work. <strong>Benicio Del Toro</strong>&#8216;s roaring, murderous self is wonderful, as is a twitchy turn by <strong>Adrien Brody</strong> as the art dealer and <strong>Tilda Swinton</strong> as a buyer. But it’s the absolute radiant, intoxicating turn by <strong>Léa Seydoux</strong> playing both muse and gardienne that’s truly glorious. She brings a fierce, Fraco sullenness that’s particularly intoxicating, lending a kind of local credence with her role to Anderson’s entire folly.</p>\n<p>The rapidity of shots, intricately designed and staged, gave rise to immediate desire to rewatch. Even the inclusion of neo-Ya Ya French &#8217;60s pop, voiced by <strong>Jarvis Cocker</strong> of Pulp, made one crave sitting down in a café, or jitterbugging to tunes on an aubergine-colored portable record player. Seen in a theatrical palace on the Mediterranean, the film exudes what it feels in one’s mind’s eye to be in a mystical France at its most romantic and surreal, a land where while even the undertakers have gone on strike the garishly painted obese streetwalkers feel the stuff of some master’s oil painting.</p>\n<p>As each storyline is drawn out – the prison artist, the 1968 student rebellion, the gangster kidnapping and food fantasy, along with tales of the magazine itself – we are treated to manifold sides of everything that one dreams about in such a landscape. Unapologetically literary, Anderson’s credits thank a pantheon of longform writers, from Mavis Gallant to James Baldwin, immediately providing a bibliography to delve into to elicit some of the more subtle real-world references.</p>\n<p>With sublime lensing by <strong>Robert Yeoman</strong> that switches aspect and palate throughout, a perfectly twee soundtrack by <strong>Alexandre Desplat</strong> augmenting the baroque pop and symphonic trifles, and<strong> Adam Stockhausen</strong>’s mindbendingly exceptional production design, this is simply heaven for anyone that wants their films to be very serious about having fun. Once again many of the animated elements that Anderson brought to life with <em>Isle of Dogs</em> and <em>Fantastic</em> <em>Mr. Fox</em> shows that his overtly manipulated visual style is a welcome mix of the intricately prepared and the wickedly haphazard. Add in a killer car chase that quite literally takes a pause where we return to where we left off and you’ve got a million different pieces to fall in love with.</p>\n<p>Yet above all, it’s the remarkable way in which Anderson’s tale is able to hold this much narrative, this much pomp and fury and fantasy and silliness, constrained somehow with the pages of his own dispatch. The different chapters are unique yet speak to one another, the timbre shifts but the tune remains the same, ever inviting a closer read yet never feeling above the audience. This is a world you’re invited in to explore, as he has done throughout his career, but with an effect that’s perhaps nowhere near as calibrated as with his latest.</p>\n<p>A symphony of excess, <em>The French Dispatch</em> is a <em>lot</em>, and I watched it mouth agape simply trying to hold on and let the images and words and performances enter my mind as if I was drinking from a fire hose. It’s a wild ride, to be sure, and given how rare it is to have an artist with such a commitment to such a loud, triumphant aesthetic it’s almost uncanny when pared against other, more commonly austere works, even those that pass off as blockbusters.</p>\n<p><em>The French Dispatch</em> is a rocket ship ride to your cinematic soul, meshing word, action and vision in one glorious bon-bon that’s both sweet and savory. It’s a film I cannot wait to visit over and over, and it’s a film that reminds that, yes, stories truly can take one to places that they never knew they wanted to be, yet are forever changed by the journey that we’re led on.</p>\n<p><strong>/Film Rating: 10 out of 10</strong></p>\n<p>The post <a rel=\"nofollow\" href=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/the-french-dispatch-review-cannes/\">&#8216;The French Dispatch&#8217; Review: Wes Anderson&#8217;s Whimsical New Masterwork is a Symphony of Excess [Cannes]</a> appeared first on <a rel=\"nofollow\" href=\"https://www.slashfilm.com\">/Film</a>.</p>\n<div class=\"feedflare\">\n<a href=\"http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/slashfilm?a=i6Nn46hq9Ck:LkVtnyQWXng:yIl2AUoC8zA\"><img 360w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 700px) 100vw, 700px\" /></p>\n<p>What&#8217;s the best way to celebrate getting back together with friends after a year being away from them? How about watching another group of friends get together to do some totally dangerous and insane stunts? <strong><em>Jackass Forever</em></strong> will deliver just that this fall with the return of <strong>Johnny Knoxville</strong>, <strong>Steve-O</strong>, <strong>Chris Pontius</strong>, <strong>Dave England</strong>, <strong>Wee Man</strong>, <strong><span class=\"m_52413673630920623spelle\">Ehren</span> <span class=\"m_52413673630920623spelle\">McGhehey</span></strong>, and <strong>Preston Lacy</strong>. Plus, as the <em>Jackass Forever</em> first look photos reveal, there are some new members getting in on the mayhem this time.<span id=\"more-682426\"></span></p>\n<h2>Jackass Forever First Look Photos</h2>\n<p><img class=\"size-medium wp-image-682438 aligncenter\" src=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/jackass-forever-knoxville-cannon-700x949.jpg\" alt=\"Jackass Forever First Look Photos\" width=\"700\" height=\"949\" srcset=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/jackass-forever-knoxville-cannon.jpg 700w, https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/jackass-forever-knoxville-cannon-360x488.jpg 360w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 700px) 100vw, 700px\" /></p>\n<p>Johnny Knoxville is back doing what he does best: throwing himself around in the craziest ways. That&#8217;s him above being launched out of a cannon while wearing some kind of winged suit. The <em>Jackass</em> franchise has never been shy about pulling off circus-esque stunts, and this is one of the oldest in the book. Though this one might seem familiar, they&#8217;ve never actually done this before.</p>\n<p><img class=\"size-medium wp-image-682434 aligncenter\" src=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/jackass-forever-bull-knoxville-700x467.jpg\" alt=\"Jackass Forever First Look Photos\" width=\"700\" height=\"467\" srcset=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/jackass-forever-bull-knoxville-700x467.jpg 700w, https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/jackass-forever-bull-knoxville-360x240.jpg 360w, https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/jackass-forever-bull-knoxville-768x512.jpg 768w, https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/jackass-forever-bull-knoxville.jpg 1000w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 700px) 100vw, 700px\" /></p>\n<p>However, there will be at least one old stunt that&#8217;s pulled from the previous <em>Jackass</em> movies, and that&#8217;s putting Johnny Knoxville in front of an angry bull. This time he&#8217;s dressed like a magician though, so there must be some kind of silly spin on the terrifying challenge that clearly went south. This kind of result is exactly why <em>Jackass Forever</em> <a href=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/jackass-final-movie-johnny-knoxville/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">will be Knoxville&#8217;s final film in the franchise</a>.</p>\n<p><img class=\"size-medium wp-image-682436 aligncenter\" src=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/jackass-forever-mimesnake-700x467.jpg\" alt=\"Jackass Forever First Look Photos\" width=\"700\" height=\"467\" srcset=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/jackass-forever-mimesnake.jpg 700w, https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/jackass-forever-mimesnake-360x240.jpg 360w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 700px) 100vw, 700px\" /></p>\n<p><em>Jackass Forever</em> will also see some new faces joining the old gang. Above, you can see <em>Jackass</em> has finally welcomed a woman into the crew in the form of comedian <strong>Rachel Wolfson</strong>. She&#8217;s also joined by fellow newcomer <strong>Sean “Poopies” McInerney</strong>, who is facing down a presumably angry snake sitting on a barrel. For good measure, they&#8217;re dressed as mimes along with Steve-O, probably just trying to give the snake a good show.</p>\n<p><img class=\"size-medium wp-image-682435 aligncenter\" src=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/jackass-forever-poopblow-700x467.jpg\" alt=\"Jackass Forever First Look Photos\" width=\"700\" height=\"467\" srcset=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/jackass-forever-poopblow-700x467.jpg 700w, https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/jackass-forever-poopblow-360x240.jpg 360w, https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/jackass-forever-poopblow-768x512.jpg 768w, https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/jackass-forever-poopblow.jpg 1000w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 700px) 100vw, 700px\" /></p>\n<p>Then there&#8217;s this potentially dangerous stunt that puts <span class=\"m_52413673630920623spelle\">Ehren</span> <span class=\"m_52413673630920623spelle\">McGhehey (now known as <strong>Danger Ehren</strong> for some reason) in a glass contraption with <em>Loiter Squad</em> cast member <strong>Dark Shark</strong>. At first I thought they were trying to blow some kind of bug away from themselves and towards the other, but upon closer inspection, it looks like that just might be a big piece of poop instead. </span></p>\n<p><img class=\"size-medium wp-image-682437 aligncenter\" src=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/jackass-forever-watertankstunt-700x467.jpg\" alt=\"Jackass Forever First Look Photos\" width=\"700\" height=\"467\" srcset=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/jackass-forever-watertankstunt-700x467.jpg 700w, https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/jackass-forever-watertankstunt-360x240.jpg 360w, https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/jackass-forever-watertankstunt-768x512.jpg 768w, https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/jackass-forever-watertankstunt.jpg 1000w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 700px) 100vw, 700px\" /></p>\n<p>Finally, we have <em>Loiter Squad</em> cast member <strong>Jasper</strong> (in the far back on the left), Sean “<span class=\"m_52413673630920623spelle\">Poopies</span>” McInerny, Johnny Knoxville, Wee Man, Steve-O, and newcomer <strong>Zach Holmes</strong> (the newest big guy on the team in the back) looking on as former <em>Mythbusters</em> team member <strong>Tory </strong><span class=\"m_52413673630920623spelle\"><strong>Bellec</strong>i</span> is doing something with newcomer <strong>Eric Manaka</strong> in this water tank with a chair in it. That chair also has straps on the legs, which is stress-inducing, but we&#8217;re honestly not sure what&#8217;s happening hear. Knoxville is dressed as a sailor, so maybe this is some kind of naval recruitment challenge?</p>\n<p>If you&#8217;re wondering where <strong>Bam Margera</strong> is in all this, to make a long story short, he was fired from the movie after his struggles with addiction and mental health creating a rift with his family and the <em>Jackass</em> crew. Margera has long struggled with substance abuse, but the death of <em>Jackass</em> crew member Ryan Dunn sent him into an even worse spiral, and it has resulted in him being unfit to appear in the franchise anymore. You can find out more about Bam Margera&#8217;s issues <a href=\"https://www.complex.com/pop-culture/jackass-bam-margera-beef-explained/margera-robbed-colombia\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">over here</a>.</p>\n<p>This certainly looks like everything we&#8217;d expect from a <em>Jackass</em> movie, and there will be plenty more to see when the first trailer arrives next week on July 20. Unfortunately, we&#8217;ll have to wait a few months after that to see all the stunts since the movie doesn&#8217;t arrive in theaters until <strong>October 22, 2021</strong>.</p>\n<p>The post <a 02:35:16","updatedTime":"2021-07-13 02:35:16","title":"The Original Theme-Park Jungle Cruise is Changing at Disneyland This Week","link":"https://www.slashfilm.com/?p=682404","description":"<p><img class=\"size-medium wp-image-655453 aligncenter\" src=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/Jungle-Cruise-ride-updates-700x300.jpg\" alt=\"Jungle Cruise ride updates\" width=\"700\" height=\"300\" srcset=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/Jungle-Cruise-ride-updates.jpg 700w, https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/Jungle-Cruise-ride-updates-360x154.jpg 360w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 700px) 100vw, 700px\" /></p>\n<p>As <strong>Disneyland</strong> gears up for its 66th anniversary on July 17, and with the arrival of the new live-action blockbuster <strong><em>Jungle Cruise</em></strong> at the end of the month, the original attraction on which the film is based is getting its moment in the spotlight with a redesign going live at the Anaheim park on July 16. Some of the changes seem intriguing, while others&#8230;.well, others are definitely changes, for better or worse.</p>\n<p><span id=\"more-682404\"></span></p>\n<p>A few days ago, the Disney Parks YouTube account posted this <a href=\"https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=KWpgLnwB_WI\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">video</a>, offering yet another glimpse at the overhaul that the <strong>Jungle Cruise</strong> is receiving, both in Orlando and in Anaheim. The video implies an interesting challenge for Disney&#8217;s Imagineers, who want to keep the ride as classic as it ever was, but also make it more relevant and inclusive, two terms that come up often in the 150-second video. (It&#8217;s a notable challenge because, unfortunately, many of the elements which have kept the Jungle Cruise &#8220;classic&#8221; are also those that make it feel dated and/or racist.)</p>\n<p>Perhaps more interesting were comments from Kim Irvine <a href=\"https://twitter.com/laughing_place/status/1413503861671690243\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">captured</a> on Twitter by the Laughing Place blog, where she mentioned that the iconic &#8220;lost team up the pole&#8221; gag — in which we see a group of explorers dangling from a pole with a rhinoceros attempting to jab at them with its pointed horn — was limited because &#8220;we didn&#8217;t relate to them&#8230;each one of them is so carefully costumed to help us understand their stories.&#8221;</p>\n<p><img class=\"aligncenter size-medium wp-image-655288\" src=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/jungle-cruise-ride-updates-700x321.jpg\" alt=\"jungle cruise ride updates\" width=\"700\" height=\"321\" srcset=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/jungle-cruise-ride-updates-700x321.jpg 700w, https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/jungle-cruise-ride-updates-360x165.jpg 360w, https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/jungle-cruise-ride-updates-768x352.jpg 768w, https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/jungle-cruise-ride-updates.jpg 948w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 700px) 100vw, 700px\" /></p>\n<h2>Change Comes for Us All</h2>\n<p>The Jungle Cruise is an attraction that has hung around the Disney Parks for more than six decades for a reason. It&#8217;s a quintessential blend of adventure and humor, of old and new technologies. But there&#8217;s no doubt that the ride has been antiquated and offensive in some respects for a long time. Change needed to come. But the balance of adding backstories where none existed, in an attraction that often lives or dies on the charm and personality of your boat&#8217;s specific skipper, with staying classic to that attraction&#8217;s roots feels like a task that Irvine and the team may not be up for.</p>\n<p>The addition of backstory may well be so easy to ignore as to be invisible. And that&#8217;s fine. If the majority of guests will simply notice that, hey, the Jungle Cruise isn&#8217;t quite so backwards-thinking anymore, that&#8217;s a good thing. Hopefully the added elements are more carefully weaved in — plenty of fans are willing to see the Jungle Cruise change without unnecessary story shoehorned in.</p>\n<p>The post <a rel=\"nofollow\" href=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/disneyland-original-jungle-cruise-ride-changes/\">The Original Theme-Park Jungle Cruise is Changing at Disneyland This Week</a> appeared first on <a rel=\"nofollow\"
